| Goal | Tool |

| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |

| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |

| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes Service Account Token Auto-Mount Audit

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes that control service account token auto-mounting: the admission controller that injects tokens, the pod spec validation that checks automountServiceAccountToken, and the token controller that creates secrets.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the security domain.

252026-03-08T22:10:22.745155agentmessage-
I am thinking...: Now I have a good understanding of the key files. Let me summarize what I've found:

1. **Admission Controller** (injects tokens):
   - `plugin/pkg/admission/serviceaccount/admission.go` - The main admission controller that:
     - Sets default service account name
     - Calls `shouldAutomount()` to check if token should be mounted
     - Calls `mountServiceAccountToken()` to inject the token volume
     - Has `TokenVolumeSource()` function
     - Has `shouldAutomount()` function that checks both pod spec and service account's `AutomountServiceAccountToken` field

2. **Token Controller** (creates secrets):
   - `pkg/controller/serviceaccount/tokens_controller.go` - The `TokensController` that:
     - Manages ServiceAccountToken secrets
     - `generateTokenIfNeeded()` - populates token data in secrets
     - `syncSecret()` - syncs secrets
     - `syncServiceAccount()` - syncs service accounts

3. **Pod Spec Validation** (checks automountServiceAccountToken):
   - `pkg/apis/core/validation/validation.go` - Contains `ValidatePodSpec()` which validates the pod spec including `serviceAccountName`
   - Also contains `ValidateServiceAccount()` and `ValidateServiceAccountUpdate()`
   - Also validates `ServiceAccountToken` projected volumes

4. **Service Account Controller**:
   - `pkg/controller/serviceaccount/serviceaccounts_controller.go` - Manages ServiceAccount objects

5. **Legacy SA Token Cleaner**:
   - `pkg/controller/serviceaccount/legacy_serviceaccount_token_cleaner.go` - Cleans up legacy SA tokens

The answer file has been created at `/workspace/answer.json`. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Key Files Found

### 1. Admission Controller (Token Injection)
**`plugin/pkg/admission/serviceaccount/admission.go`**
- The `Plugin` struct implements the `ServiceAccount` admission controller
- `Admit()` — mutating handler that injects tokens into pods
- `shouldAutomount(sa, pod)` — checks `pod.Spec.AutomountServiceAccountToken` (pod wins) then `sa.AutomountServiceAccountToken`, defaulting to `true`
- `mountServiceAccountToken()` — injects the projected volume at `/var/run/secrets/kubernetes.io/serviceaccount`
- `TokenVolumeSource()` — builds the projected volume with SA token, CA cert, and namespace

### 2. Pod Spec Validation
**`pkg/apis/core/validation/validation.go`**
- `ValidatePodSpec()` — validates `serviceAccountName` format and projected `ServiceAccountToken` volume parameters (expiration bounds, path requirements)
- `ValidateServiceAccount()` / `ValidateServiceAccountUpdate()` — validates service account objects
- Also validates `SecretTypeServiceAccountToken` secrets

### 3. Token Controller (Secret Creation)
**`pkg/controller/serviceaccount/tokens_controller.go`**
- `TokensController` — manages legacy `ServiceAccountToken`-type secrets
- `generateTokenIfNeeded()` — signs and populates JWT token data in secrets
- `syncSecret()` / `syncServiceAccount()` — event-driven reconciliation loops

### Supporting Files
- `pkg/controller/serviceaccount/serviceaccounts_controller.go` — ensures `default` SA exists in every namespace
- `pkg/controller/serviceaccount/legacy_serviceaccount_token_cleaner.go` — cleans up unused legacy tokens
- `pkg/controller/serviceaccount/tokengetter.go` — provides token getter for authenticator
- `cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/core.go` — wi

The answer file is complete and valid. The task has been fully completed. Here's a summary of what was found and documented in `/workspace/answer.json`:

## Summary of Findings

The Kubernetes service account token auto-mounting system in `kubernetes/kubernetes` (v1.32.0) is controlled by three primary Go source files:

### 1. Admission Controller — `plugin/pkg/admission/serviceaccount/admission.go`
The central file for token auto-mounting. The `Plugin` struct intercepts Pod CREATE requests:
- **`shouldAutomount()`** — implements the precedence logic: pod-level `AutomountServiceAccountToken` overrides SA-level, defaulting to `true`
- **`mountServiceAccountToken()`** — injects the projected volume at `/var/run/secrets/kubernetes.io/serviceaccount`
- **`TokenVolumeSource()`** — builds the projected volume with SA token, CA cert, and namespace
- **`Admit()`** / **`Validate()`** — the mutating and validating admission handlers

### 2. Pod Spec Validation — `pkg/apis/core/validation/validation.go`
- **`ValidatePodSpec()`** — validates `serviceAccountName` format and projected `ServiceAccountToken` volume parameters (expiration bounds 10min–2^32s, path requirements)
- **`ValidateServiceAccount()`** / **`ValidateServiceAccountUpdate()`** — validates service account objects
- Also validates `SecretTypeServiceAccountToken` secrets

### 3. Token Controller — `pkg/controller/serviceaccount/tokens_controller.go`
The `TokensController` manages legacy `ServiceAccountToken`-type secrets:
- **`generateTokenIfNeeded()`** — signs and populates JWT token data in secrets
- **`syncSecret()`** / **`syncServiceAccount()`** — event-driven reconciliation loops
- **`NewTokensController()`** — wires up informers for ServiceAccounts and Secrets

Supporting files include `serviceaccounts_controller

A Pod is created \u2192 `ServiceAccount` admission plugin `Admit()` is called.\\n2. `shouldAutomount()` checks `pod.Spec.AutomountServiceAccountToken` (pod wins) then `sa.AutomountServiceAccountToken` (SA-level), defaulting to `true`.\\n3. If automounting is enabled, `mountServiceAccountToken()` injects a projected volume with a bound service account token, CA cert, and namespace into the pod spec.\\n4. Separately, the `TokensController` watches for `ServiceAccountToken`-type secrets and calls `generateTokenIfNeeded()` to sign and populate legacy token secrets (for older clients that request them explicitly).\\n5. `ValidatePodSpec()` in `pkg/apis/core/validation/validation.go` validates the `serviceAccountName` field and projected `ServiceAccountToken` volume parameters.\"\n}\n",
